I was in an accident about a year and a half ago and didn't have rental coverage, so I held off on repairs until I could decide what to do. I saw that CARSTAR La Habra offers free 10 day rentals if your damages exceed $599, and they work with most insurances, and I was sold!

I called and set an appointment with Todd, who was super helpful in guiding me through the insurance process and setting me up with my rental. He did all the communications with my insurance so I wouldn't have to, all I had to do was  provide my insurance and the claim number. The entire drop off procedure took no more than 10 minutes. While I waited for Enterprise to pick me up I saw that he prepped my car by spraying disinfectant (great during COVID!) and put protective covers inside my car on my steering wheel and my seat and floors.

Sean did my estimate and was in charge of the repairs on my car, and he was extremely reassuring that my vehicle would come out like new, and I'm glad I trusted him, it came out amazing! Between Sean and Kevin (the body man who worked on my car) my car came out just as nice as when I bought it, I couldn't be happier! They worked on getting it done within the short timeline I had and were very communicative during the process so I was aware of what was being done and what was damaged!

Finally, when I went to pick up my car, Huy helped me get checked out and instead of having to return my rental to Enterprise, he took my keys and said they'd call the rental place to come pick it up, and I was able to quickly pick up my car and head home! I was thoroughly pleased with my experience here, I've seen many great reviews and they definitely met and exceeded my expectations. < Review>
We chose Amazing Cakes as our wedding cake vendor. The store is on the smaller side and it's a family-ran business. The cake was a 4-tier cake with two alternating flavors. The design is simple, as requested by us, since we want to decorate with real flowers. Amazing Cakes doesn't provide flowers nor cake stand, so we provided our own cake stand and our florist decorated the cake. They have the option to decorate the cake for your, but your florist will need to drop off the flowers the day before (which did not work for our schedule). The cake was very tasty and moist, and not as sweet as other cake vendors I have tasted (to my liking).

However, I would say they may not be the most organized. We spoke with one person about the arrangement for a birthday cake for a 1 year old on our wedding day on the side during our Tasting Appointment. When we call back to confirm we would like to contract with them, the first person was not available so we had to speak with another person, who was highly confused about this arrangement. When they called a week before my wedding to confirm headcount, they were again confused about the birthday cake arrangement.

I just felt that communication could have been better, but no big deal. Overall I would still recommend Amazing Cakes. I look forward to coming back for our one-year anniversary cake.< /Review>

Nice little frozen yogurt shop.  It is make your own, so you control how much or little you want of yogurt, ice cream, sorbet or toppings.  Pricey if you don't belong to their rewards program.  Always clean.  Sometimes not a lot of variety or too many flavors that aren't ready (soupy).  Somewhere along the line they stopped stacking coupons, so I couldn't use all my coupons before they expired.  If you earn the unlimited cup, it can be hard to load up as they don't have wafers or cookies with which to build a "retaining wall".  Family friendly, autism friendly,  handicap accessible.  Ample free parking.< /Text>

We had a Groupon deal which consisted of a soup or salad ( we chose the soup - clam chowder), wood over crab, and a chocolate cake. < review>
IG: eatgosee
This was somewhat of an astonishing experience. But before we get to that let‚Äôs set the scene.
This is a large restaurants positions firmly on the waterfront with a view looking out into the bay. It has a very vibrant decor with a clear Fishermans, nautical theme. It is placed on a very busy thoroughfare in a touristy and popular area of San Francisco. Needless to say it is the type of area where you would expect to see a lot of people milling around, walking by and therefore for traffic coming into this restaurant. We came here once for lunch but I walked past it several times in the days following.

HIGHLIGHTS:
- Location as there is plenty of good atmosphere if you‚Äôre sitting outside. The inside is very bright and something closer to a Disney meets theme restaurant.

DIVIDED:
- Half of the group had the red snapper dish which I understand was quite good but admittedly did not try myself. The house rose that we drank was also perfectly drinkable and if you came here to only have a bottle of ros√© while sitting outside and watching the world go by, you would probably have quite a good experience.

LOWLIGHTS:
- SERVICE. This is where the tipping culture in the United States really drives the wrong behaviour. I‚Äôll wait I got the order wrong, the food arrived five minutes before the wind it (which is in excusable given one thing requires cooking and the other thing requires simply picking up on pouring), it took forever to get waiters to come see us. Not with standing the fact that this is a large restaurant it is also at the time that we were here only about 20% full during lunch in the middle of the week. i‚Äôm not entirely sure why as paying guests we need to pay even the minimum culturally acceptable amount of service charge for an experience that frankly was inferior to whether I got up and went to the bar and into the kitchen to retrieve the things that I ordered.

- Clam chowder bowl: Admittedly this is not the kind of food that I particularly enjoy but, when in Rome, we decided to have the Klamm chowder because it felt like the right thing to do and also because it was recommended someone strongly from the waiter. The soup was floury, it arrived in a bread bowl which I know is customary but borders on pointless given that nobody eats the bread bowl (three of the tables around us did the same thing and I noticed that they did not eat at either - it seems like a waste of bread). It arrived with a side salad which is not presented in any particularly attractive way and looking through the leaves some of them appear to be old and not picked through by the kitchen.

Should I come here again? Hopefully not. And then here I suspect lies the issue. As this restaurant is positioned on a popular thoroughfare, I question how many returning guests actually come back to this place. It does not seem fair to call this a tourist trap but it is not far away from that. There are a lot of very basic and elementary mistakes systematically made here that requires thoughtful attention. If there is as much effort was put into the food and service as it has into the decor then this could be a very good place with lines around the corner. After all this is a city where people do lineup around the corner to get into a good restaurant but, as mentioned, this place was only 20% full during lunchtime on a sunny day in a touristy area which makes me ask questions.</review>

<review>I was trying this place with my son to see how it is.  I was told 10 minutes or more waiting time. It was 33 minutes actually.  Was finally sat down and waited another 10 minutes to see who our waiter was.  No water, no I'll be right with you.  It was busy but there was no organization at all of the waitstaff.  No one seemed to have a designated station. And at one point, I noticed there a person who seemed like a waiter just walking around without a purpose.  Finally, our waiter came and I immediately ordered two pizzas. That came out a little late but not too bad.

The food:  First, they brought out sliced day-old bread with butter. The pepperoni pizza:  The crust was good but the pizza was greasy and very salty, more than normal for pepperoni.  Our waiter never came back.  I asked another waitstaff for check and I had to call several waiters so they could take my credit card.  Finally, our waiter came back and rung us up.

The decor:  It is very antiquated and some of the chairs were cheap plastic patio chairs.   And the restaurant had a distinct odor of stale beer.

Overall:  This is more of a bar with overpriced bar food.  Do not expect more than that.   Waitstaff is very inexperienced and the person who seemed to be the manager managed nothing.   And I'm still laughing at the sliced bread they served.  I was shaking my head.   Caveat emptor!!!<//review><Name>Francisco ‚ÄúEddie‚Äù<//Name></record></dataset><record>

< text>
After a long trip driving from Yosemite National Park to San Francisco, we were looking for a place to eat dinner, but more importantly, a place that would let us use the bathroom.  After being refused the use of a bathroom FOUR TIMES at other Fisherman's Wharf restaurants, we were VERY WELCOMED at Capurro's by the owner, Paul.  He gladly allowed the use of the bathroom even before he knew we were going to eat there.  His hospitality was warm and friendly, as we were weary travelers on the road most of the day.  Additionally, our server, Raluca, was the sweetest, most professional and efficient waitresses we had on our 12-day vacation in California (we are from Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania).  Our meal was INCREDIBLE and very affordable!  There were six of us eating and no one was disappointed.  I highly recommend this restaurant if in the area.  Ask to meet Paul, too.  He will make you feel like you are at home.  Our only disappointment was we wanted to tell Paul how much we enjoyed our meal (and we wanted to get a picture with him), but he left for the night.  I hope you are reading this review so you know what a wonderful establishment you are running!< /text>

The atmosphere and location and service are womderful! Really a fun place. The food was just eh. The chowder in a bread bowl was great! The fries were pretty good too. The "salad" though was just lettuce and dressing with about 4 croutons. That isn't a salad. Anyone can put dressing on plain romaine lettuce...still not a salad. The crab panini wasn't good. It tasted more like coleslaw that crab meat. It was cold with rubbery cheese on top and the crab was mixed up with some watery mayonnaise like stuff. Unimpressed there. I probably wouldn't go back, but you can definitely try some other menu items and maybe you'll have better luck.<//review>

< review>
This restaurant looks nice, the staff is okay but the food is pretty meh bordering on sub par. My friend and I made the mistake of ordering some of the higher priced items on the menu and they just did not justify the price.

He asked for his steak medium rare but, even from the most generous standpoint it was maybe _at best_ medium well, if not well. He stated it was full of gristle and generally not good. He was overcharged for the meal as well.

I went for a safer chicken parm, this wasn't awful, but the plate was a total mess. Typically you would wipe the rim of a plate, but this one had sauce all over it that found its way on my shirt several times.

I would rate this 5/5 if the price was, say, 30-40% less, but given the price point it was really not worth it.

If you do visit, stick to a burger or something simple, it feels like that is where they would probably shine.<//review>

Good choice for seafood and Italian in Fisherman's Wharf. Food was very good. We had fresh fish, shrimp, and marinated whole crab. It all had good flavor, well balanced seasonings and correct temperature. The 4/5 is for service. The waiter was friendly but inattentive. We had to call him over for just about everything (water, get the bill, pickup the bill, bring back the credit card to sign, etc.). Prices are SF average (which is to say high compared to other parts of the U.S. but on par for San Francisco). FYI: the place is LOUD. I don't recommend this for an intimate dinner for two (if you want to hear each other that is).< /Review>

< rate>

<Text>My wife and I had just spent time on the Hyde St. Pier and were ready for an early dinner.  We were attracted by the vibrant colors of the building and the wooden sailor out front.  The interior is just as striking with the walls covered with photos and memorabilia of the history of the fishing industry in San Francisco.  Our waitress was sweet and very attentive.  Got us started on drinks and delicious sourdough bread right away.  We decided to   go with some small plates and chowder.  We ordered Bruschetta, crab cakes,  crab cocktail and clam chowder.  The Bruschetta  was very good!  The tomatoes had the perfect balance of sweetness and acid, the bread toasted perfectly.  The crab cakes were great.  Tons of very fresh Dungeness crab, seasoned perfectly.  Slightly crispy on the outside.  Really good.  The crab cocktail was a standout.  They serve the crab separately on a bed of lettuce with the sauce on the side.  I was surprised at how generous they are with the very fresh Dungeness crab.  Big chunks of succulent lump crab.  The sauce was the perfect compliment.   Zingy but not overly spicy. The New England Clam Chowder was hearty and very well seasoned.  Very generous with the clams.  Not quite as good as Alioto's #8 but quite good.  One highlight of the meal was meeting the owner.  He visited several tables, including ours and he was very charming.   Obviously very proud of his restaurant.  I love to see a really engaged owner and his commitment shows in their food.<//Text>< pictures>

<Review>Did not get a chance to eat here but was looks like a good place.< /Review>< GmapID>
0x808580e1a91a59b1:0xb267be4b653d9796</GmapID>
<Name>R J< /Name></record></dataset><record>
<pictures>None< /pictures><user>105277346814950960603</user><gmapID>0x808580e1a91a59b1:0xb267be4b653d9796< /gmapID><time>1369937908443<//time>< Review>
We went to Capurro's using a Groupon and still got excellent service!  The waiter and staff were very attentive.  We ordered calamari as an extra appetizer and we both felt it was the best we have ever had.  The New England style clam chowder was excellent as was the stonewood fired crab!  I usually like the cold crab with clarified butter but decided to try it warmed in white wine and herbs.  It was awesome that way!  There was no "fishiness" at all and it was plenty.  (I'll try to prepare it that way at home to avoid the calories of all the butter!)  For the dessert they served tiramisu which was just ok.  I had read other reviews about the dessert that was not tiramisu (not my favorite dessert anyway) and was disappointed that we did not get that, but I was full anyway and did not need all the calories!  We also had cocktails that were only $5 each which I felt was very reasonable for SF.  It was well bourbon but still a good value!  We would definitely dine there again.</Review>
